[1mูุฌููุนุงุช ุงูุฃุนูุงู ูุงููุชุจ ุงูููุฏูุฉ ููุชุจ ุงูุณูุฑ ุงูุฐุงุชูุฉ ุงูุนุงูุฉ [0m

Indispensable to Rousseau scholarship today are two major publishing ventures of the past forty years, the Plรฉiade edition of his [3m
ลuvres complรจtes [0m, compiled by B. Gagnebin, M. Raymond, and others (Paris, 1959โ95), and the Voltaire Foundation edition of his [3m
Correspondance complรจte [0m, by R. A. Leigh (Geneva and Oxford, 1965โ98). Each is drawn from the original manuscripts and is richly 
documented with editorial notes, illustrating Rousseauโs sources and parallel passages across his writings. The long-awaited fifth 
volume of the Plรฉiade [3mลuvres complรจtes [0membraces most of his works on music and language, including the [3mDictionnaire de musique [0mand 
other texts never before published with a scholarly introduction or footnotes, although its fine edition of the [3mEssai sur 
lโorigine des langues [0mby Jean Starobinski has been available for some time separately (Paris, 1990) and the same text was even 
earlier accorded extensive annotation by Charles Porset (2nd edn, Bordeaux, 1970). Of Rousseauโs principal works incorporated in 
the Plรฉiade edition, perhaps only the [3mDiscours sur les sciences et les arts [0mis presented with more compelling command of its 
sources elsewhere, by George Havens (New York, 1946). Equally noteworthy is the edition, including a German translation, of the [3m
Discours sur lโinรฉgalitรฉ [0mby Heinrich Meier (Paderborn, 1984). The extensively annotated translation of Rousseauโs [3mCollected 
Writings [0m(Hanover, NH, 1990โ ) currently in progress under the general supervision of Roger Masters and Christopher Kelly, when 
finished, should provide the best, and in several instances the first, editions of his works for English readers. Of the major 
writings, including the [3mDiscours sur lโinรฉgalitรฉ [0m, the [3mContrat social [0m, the [3mConfessions [0m, and the [3mRรชveries [0m, there are numerous, 
often fine, translations into English, including those contained in the series of Texts in the History of Political Thought 
(Cambridge University Press) and the Worldโs Classics series (Oxford University Press). Leighโs edition of the [3mCorrespondance 
complรจte [0m, in fifty-two volumes, is one of the most remarkable works of modern scholarship in any fieldโits annotation majestic, 
its powers of resuscitating Rousseauโs world, and even the spontaneity and refinement of the composition of his ideas, 
unsurpassed. 

This correspondence, and Rousseauโs own [3mConfessions [0m, have helped make it possible for Raymond Trousson and Maurice Cranston to 
produce perhaps the finest biographies of Rousseau in any language (Paris, 1988 and 1989; and London, 1983, 1991, and 1997), 
although Cranston did not survive to complete his third volume. Jean Guรฉhennoโs [3mJean-Jacques Rousseau [0m(Eng. trans., 2 vols, 
London, 1966) and Lester Crockerโs [3mJean-Jacques Rousseau [0m(2 vols, New York, 1968 and 1973) form substantial and notable 
biographies as well. Ronald Grimsleyโs [3mJean-Jacques Rousseau: A Study of Self-Awareness [0m(2nd edn, Cardiff, 1969) offers a 
particularly sensitive treatment of the development of Rousseauโs personality through his writings, while Kellyโs [3mRousseauโs 
Exemplary Life: The โConfessionsโ as Political Philosophy [0m(Ithaca, NY, 1987) shrewdly interprets the autobiography in the light of 
Rousseauโs principles. 

Among English-language commentaries on his thought in different genres, Ernst Cassirerโs [3mThe Question of Jean-Jacques Rousseau [0m
(2nd edn, New Haven, Conn., 1989), Judith Shklarโs [3mMen and Citizens: A Study of Rousseauโs Social Theory [0m(2nd edn, Cambridge, 
1985), and C. W. Hendelโs more comprehensive [3mJean-Jacques Rousseau: Moralist [0m(2nd edn, Indianapolis, 1962) excel, Hendelโs work in 
particular being among the most subtly detailed accounts of Rousseauโs philosophy in any language. Of comparable quality, showing 
equal mastery of Rousseauโs writings across several disciplines, is Timothy OโHaganโs [3mRousseau [0m(London and New York, 1999). In 
French, the most remarkable treatments of his thought are probably Bronisลaw Baczkoโs [3mRousseau: Solitude et communautรฉ [0m, 
originally published in Polish (Paris 1974), Pierre Burgelinโs [3mLa Philosophie de lโexistence de J. J. Rousseau [0m(2nd edn, Paris, 
1973), and Starobinskiโs classic study, dating from 1957, now available in English, [3mJean-Jacques Rousseau: Transparency and 
Obstruction [0m(Chicago, 1988), which is dazzling in its images of Rousseauโs inner experience and metaphors of opaque reflection. 

John Hope Mason, in [3mThe Indispensable Rousseau [0m(London, 1979), offers English readers a skilful single-volume commentary, 
interwoven with selections from almost all of Rousseauโs major writings, while N. J. H. Dent, in [3mA Rousseau Dictionary [0m(Oxford, 
1992), provides a well-conceived thematic treatment of Rousseauโs works, with useful pointers in each case to the pertinent 
secondary literature. The massively authoritative [3mDictionnaire de Jean-Jacques Rousseau [0m(Paris, 1996), published under the 
direction of Trousson and Frรฉdรฉric Eigeldinger, is comprised of 700 entries by almost one hundred authors, addressed to writings, 
subjects, places, and persons. The Sociรฉtรฉ Jean-Jacques Rousseau, based in Geneva, has since 1905 produced a journal of remarkable 
erudition, the [3mAnnales [0m, and for those who find that they can never have enough of Rousseau, there is a computer-generated [3m
Collection des index et concordances [0mof his writings still in progress (Geneva and Paris, 1977โ ), under the general supervision 
of Michel Launay and dedicated colleagues at the University of Nice and elsewhere. Scholars who consult the two volumes thus far 
published of the [3mBibliography of the writings of Rousseau to 1800 [0mby Jo-Ann McEachern (Oxford, 1989 and 1993) will be richly

Despite a rapidly growing number of treatments of particular themes within and around his philosophy of music, there is still much
